So Bailey you were kind of right but also not really. ğŸ˜…  "The old military revolver, specifically the Colt Single Action Army, was called the "Peacemaker" because the idea was that its presence could deter conflict and act as an equalizer, meaning that even a smaller or weaker person could defend themselves, thus promoting a sense of peace by discouraging aggression; the name is attributed to a quote from Samuel Colt himself, the gun's inventor, who said that his arms were the "best peacemakers"."

This is going to be an unpopular opinion, but I don't think Bryan should have been charged at all. I dont believe in punishing people for trying to convince other people to commit crimes, because ultimately those people made the conscious decision to listen to them and commit a crime. This is basically punishing someone for speech.   Now there are certain cases that might be an exception, such as the person being influenced being a child or mentally disabled or hindered in some way, but generally i feel like punishing people for suggesting or trying to convince someone to commit a crime is wrong and sets the precedent that the person who actually committed a crime isnt 100% accountable, which is inaccurate. The only person who should be punished in a crime is the person who committed the crime. That's it.

Beginning in the Wild West era through the American Civil War, all the way to the sets of some of the most iconic Hollywood Western movies, this legendary gun-shaped the entire culture. The Peacemaker was so much more than just one of the best-designed guns of the era.  It was this weapon that made the difference in the westward expansion by providing the much-needed protection of pioneers in the West. Additionally, it paved the way for the production of multi-shot firearms, which eventually would transform the United States into a global power.

In reference to the gun, the Peacemaker was a single-action revolver. You need to manually pull back the hammer on a single-action revolver before firing. This also allowed people to "fan" which is holding down the trigger and continually pulling back on the hammer. This wasn't done often because it was incredibly inaccurate to do, it used up ammo super fast (you only have six shots), and it wasn't uncommon to accidentally get that piece of skin between your thumb and index finger caught, which would hurt like an MFer.   Modern handguns are dual-action, which means you don't pull back the hammer (despite them doing this in movies) as pulling the trigger does both actions for you. Some guns don't even have an external hammer (Glocks, for instance) yet you'll still hear that tell-tale "chk-chk" sound whenever someone raises and aims a gun in a movie. It's become a trope and it's incredibly inaccurate, but probably stems from westerns where manually cocking the hammer was needed if the film was trying to be at all realistic.   Then again, there are so many inaccurate ideas about firearms I wouldn't even know where to begin debunking them. Not all of these are from movies or TV shows either, but ideas people really believe in real life. For instance, a lot of people get all concerned when they hear the term "semi-automatic" and seem to equate that with "automatic." Not true. Semi-automatic is simply the ammunition cycling mechanism. In other words, every time you press the trigger, one shot fires. Virtually all handguns are like this.   You might ask, "But doesn't every gun do that when you pull the trigger?" Nope. There are numerous types of cycling mechanisms. Examples include muzzle loading, breech loading, lever-action, bolt-action, straight-pull action, pump action, and this doesn't even get into really old firearm mechanisms, like flintlocks, wheellocks, matchlocks, and caplocks. Certain terms sound scary, but they're really not and even if you're not interested in firearms, understanding the mechanics of how they work is fascinating.   I have tons of information about firearms, not because I am a "gun nut" but because I find the history of weapons (which goes way beyond firearms) and the science involved in inventing and making them work incredibly interesting.

Fun Fact! The model P, or "Peacemaker", was standard issue in the US Army for a time. Wyatt Earp also famously carried one during his time as a law man in Dodge City! The nickname is partly attributed to the firing power of the weapon, as one shot from the Model P would be enough to stop the fighting and make peace. Either because your rival was now dead, or so terrified of the power of the gun that they no longer wanted anything to do with you.

The "peacemaker" has a very glorious history. And deserves to be told. I'll try to keep it short. In 1859 Samual Colt came out with a 6 shot.32 revolver called the "Navy Revolver" . The Gun of choice for Robert E Lee & Doc Holliday. However, in 1870 Smith & Wesson's patent ran out. and the army offered a contract for a .45 6-shot. so Colt redesigned his Navy .32 and made it a shorter version that weighed a little more  and was longer. But most importantly it shot metal bullets instead of paper ones (yes paper ones). .444-.40 ones were sold to civilians.  This was the gun of choice for Theodore Roosevelt and Wyatt Earp. it's called the "Peacemaker" beacause it is said to be the gun that won the west. In 1941 Colt stopped production of the civilian version of the Peacemaker for the war. However after the war it was considered old fashioned and outdated. But it was popular again by western movies so in 1956 Colt started production again of many different models, barrel lengths and calibers and is still in production to this day.

The Peacemaker was one of the most popular arms for the time because it was reliable. The single action (need to pull the hammer to set the trigger and rotate the cylinder) required fewer parts and was easier to manufacture compared to a double action (single trigger pull rotates the cylinder and sets/ fires a round). Actually more accurate as less force is needed to pull the trigger, and with training can be fired as fast as a double action.

Peacemaker is just a name they gave a certain gun b/c most sheriffs carried back in the day... Also, having to pull the "hammer" back to fire the gun, is called a "double action", meaning you have to pull the hammer and then pull the trigger. Semi-auto and automatic guns now of days are mostly single action. A hammer was needed to hit the flint to fire the gun, that's why it's on all older style guns.
